# Validator Take

Validator take is the share of delegated-stake emissions that a validator keeps before the remaining
emissions flow to stakers
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

The term is a distribution concept. It describes a split inside delegated-stake emissions after the
validator-side amount already exists, not the consensus step that produced that amount
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## What It Represents

Validator take concerns the portion of emissions tied to delegated stake on a selected subnet. On
netuid 1, the key relationship is between a validator and the stakers who delegated to it: the take
is the validator's kept share, and the remaining delegated-stake emissions flow to those stakers at
tempo distribution ([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Tempo](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#tempo),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Examples tied to netuid 1 illustrate one subnet's commission split. They should not be read as
representing production settings on another network
([Bittensor Networks](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/concepts/bittensor-networks)).

## Distinction from Subnet Owner Take

On a subnet such as netuid 1, validator take and subnet owner take name different emission slices.
Validator take is the percentage a validator keeps from delegated-stake dividends before the
remainder flows to nominators, while subnet owner take is the documented 18 percent share of subnet
alpha emissions routed to the subnet owner as stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Validator take** — validator–delegator split on validation dividends at tempo distribution.
- **Subnet owner take** — global owner cut from that subnet's emission bucket.

## Distinction from Child Hotkeys

Validator take names the commission rate on validation dividends on a subnet such as netuid 1, while
a child hotkey names the authorized key a parent delegate uses to perform validation with
re-delegated stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — fee applied when dividends split between validator and stakers.
- **Child hotkey** — worker identity that earns dividends under delegation.

## Distinction from Dividends

Validator take is the share of validator dividends kept by the validator hotkey. Dividends are the
validator-side reward stream produced from subnet emissions before that split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Dividends](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#emission)).

- **Dividends** — validator-side payout category consensus produces.
- **Validator take** — configured share kept from the delegated-stake portion at distribution.

## Distinction from Childkey Take

A child hotkey carries its own take rate, the [[Childkey Take]], which applies at a different point
in the dividend flow. Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from emissions tied to
delegated stake before the remainder reaches delegators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — split between validator and its delegators.
- **[[Childkey Take]]** — split between parent hotkey and child hotkey validating on its behalf.

## Distinction from Validator Permit

Validator take is the commission on delegated-stake dividends. A validator permit is the on-chain
right to submit counting weights and take part in consensus
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Validator Permit](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-permit)).

- **Validator permit** — right to submit counting weights before dividends exist.
- **Validator take** — commission applied once delegated-stake dividends are credited.

## Distinction from Effective Stake

Effective stake is the combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey. Validator take is the
commission rate applied when delegated-emission returns are split at distribution
([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Effective stake** — combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey.
- **Validator take** — commission rate on delegated returns at distribution.

## Distinction from Nominator

A nominator delegates TAO to a validator hotkey. Validator take names what share of
delegated-emission returns the validator keeps before the remainder flows to those nominators
([Glossary: Nominator](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#nominator),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Nominator** — role that supplies delegated support.
- **Validator take** — configured share the validator keeps before the remainder flows to stakers.

## Distinction from Delegation Rewards

Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from delegated-emission returns before nominators
receive the remainder, while delegation rewards are what remains for delegated stake after that
split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Validator take** — cut taken off the top of delegated returns.
- **Delegation rewards** — portion that reaches nominators afterward.

## Distinction from Emission Split

Validator take is not a fourth headline share in the emission split. It is the cut a validator keeps
from delegated stake inside the validator-and-staker bucket after that bucket is credited
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Emission split** — role proportions credited at tempo end.
- **Validator take** — commission applied inside the validator-and-staker bucket.

## Distinction from Incentives

[Incentives](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#incentives) name miner-side emission
outcomes produced from clipped and aggregated weight signals. Validator take names the configured
share a validator keeps when the delegated-stake portion is later split
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus)).

- **Incentives** — miner-side emission outcomes from consensus.
- **Validator take** — validator commission on delegated-stake dividends at distribution.

## Distinction from Yuma Consensus

Validator take is the configurable commission a validator keeps from delegated-stake emissions at
distribution. It names a post-settlement split rule inside the staking relationship, not the
consensus mechanism that builds validator dividend shares from weight submissions
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

Yuma Consensus is the on-chain mechanism that runs at the epoch boundary on the selected netuid. It
reads the weight matrix from eligible validators, applies clipping and bonding, and converts the
result into miner incentives and validator dividend shares
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions)).

Yuma produces the validator-side dividend pool from consensus; validator take applies afterward when
the delegated-stake portion is split between validator and nominators. Settlement and commission are
separate stages on the same emission path
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Readers should not read a higher take percentage as proof of stronger weight influence—that is stake
weight vocabulary. Take only governs how delegated dividends are shared after Yuma settles.

- **Validator take** — commission on delegated-stake validator emissions at distribution.
- **Yuma Consensus** — epoch-boundary settlement from validator weights to emission shares.

## Distinction from Staking

Validator take belongs to the staking relationship between a validator and the stakers who support
that validator. Delegation describes the support relationship, while validator take describes the
validator-kept share of the delegated-stake emissions
([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Delegate stake / effective stake** — stake context around a validator.
- **Validator take** — how the delegated-stake emission share is split at distribution.

## Reader Boundary

Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## Distinction from Delegate

Validator take and delegate name a fee and the party that charges it. A delegate is a validator that
accepts stake from nominators and validates on their behalf, while validator take is the percentage
that delegate keeps from the rewards generated on delegated stake before the remainder is paid to
nominators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Delegate](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Delegate** — a validator that accepts stake from nominators.
- **Validator take** — the commission that delegate keeps from delegated-stake rewards.

## Further Reading

- [Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)
- [Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)
- [Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)
- [Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)

# Contributing To Taopedia Articles

Thanks for improving Taopedia. This repository is for article content only. Website code, UI,
routing, and deployment config belong in:

https://github.com/e35ventura/taopedia

## Quick Start

1. Fork or branch from `test`.
2. Add or edit an article under `content/pages/<slug>/index.mdx`.
3. Use the required front matter.
4. Keep the article factual, concise, and Bittensor-focused.
5. Open a pull request targeting `test`.

Before opening a PR, run:

```bash
npm run format:check
npm run validate
```

## File Layout

```txt
content/pages/<slug>/index.mdx
```

Use lowercase slugs with words separated by underscores when possible:

```txt
content/pages/yuma_consensus/index.mdx
content/pages/dynamic_tao/index.mdx
```

Place images beside the article and reference them with relative paths:

```txt
content/pages/dynamic_tao/
  index.mdx
  emission-flow.png
```

```mdx
![Emission flow](./emission-flow.png)
```

## Required Front Matter

```mdx
---
title: "Dynamic TAO"
summary: "How Dynamic TAO changes subnet tokenomics and incentive allocation in Bittensor."
category: "Tokenomics"
tags: ["TAO", "Subnets"]
---
```

Required fields:

- `title`: Human-readable article title.
- `summary`: One sentence, preferably under 180 characters.
- `category`: One primary topic. Do not use `Bittensor` as a catch-all category.
- `tags`: Zero to three specific topic tags. Do not use `Bittensor`; every published Taopedia
  article is already Bittensor-focused.

Optional fields:

- `featured`: `true` for especially important pages.
- `draft`: `true` to keep unfinished work out of normal publication.
- `infoboxTitle`: Title shown in the article infobox.
- `infoboxCaption`: Short caption below the infobox image.
- `infoboxImage`: URL or local image path.
- `infoboxRows`: List of short `{ label, value }` rows.

## Bittensor Scope

Taopedia is Bittensor-centric. Good topics include:

- TAO
- wallets, coldkeys, and hotkeys
- staking and delegation
- validators and miners
- Yuma Consensus
- Dynamic TAO
- subnets and incentive mechanisms
- Bittensor governance, emissions, and operations

The Taopedia app publishes every article that is not marked `draft: true`. Articles must be
Bittensor-focused; general sample articles should not be added to this repository. Categories can be
added over time without changing the website sync logic.

## Writing Style

- Write for builders, validators, miners, and TAO holders.
- Be factual and direct.
- Define terms before using jargon heavily.
- Prefer short sections with clear headings.
- Avoid repeating the same definition, claim, or caveat.
- Cut generic blockchain, AI, decentralization, or crypto filler unless it directly explains the
  Bittensor topic.
- Keep sentences direct; do not use a long explanation when a short one preserves the meaning.
- Every section should add a new fact, distinction, caveat, source, or operational detail.
- Use `[[Article Title]]` for internal links.
- Cite official docs or primary sources when making claims.
- Link relevant codebases, source files, releases, or commits when describing implementation
  behavior.
- Avoid price predictions, investment advice, hype, or unsupported claims.

## Sources

Sources are required for factual and technical claims. AI-assisted writing is allowed, but unsourced
writing is not.

Preferred sources:

1. Current implementation code, official protocol repos, and release notes.
2. Official Bittensor/OpenTensor docs.
3. Maintainer-authored specs or documentation.
4. Reputable third-party explainers for background only.

When docs and code disagree, code is the source of truth for implementation behavior. Docs can
support conceptual explanations, but exact mechanics should be backed by code, release notes, or
official specs.

Do not use generic homepages, SEO pages, social posts, or screenshots as support for technical
claims unless they are clearly marked as context and no stronger source exists.

## Internal Links

Use wiki-style links:

```mdx
See [[Yuma Consensus]] and [[Dynamic TAO]].
```

The app resolves these links to Taopedia article pages and uses them to build backlinks.

## Infobox Example

```yaml
infoboxTitle: Dynamic TAO
infoboxCaption: Subnet tokenomics and emissions.
infoboxRows:
  - label: Network
    value: Bittensor
  - label: Asset
    value: TAO
  - label: Related
    value: "[[Subnets]]"
```

Keep infobox values short. Use the main article body for explanation.

## Pull Request Checklist

- Required front matter is present.
- The article is in `content/pages/<slug>/index.mdx`.
- The topic is Bittensor-related or intentionally marked as a sample/reference page.
- Internal links use `[[...]]`.
- Sources are included for technical or factual claims.
- Codebase links are included when implementation behavior is described.
- The article avoids repeated information and unnecessary filler.
- Images are local or from trusted sources.
- Spelling and grammar have been checked.
- `npm run format:check` succeeds if dependencies are installed.
- `npm run build:index` succeeds if dependencies are installed.

## Deployment

Merging to `test` validates and stages article changes without updating production. Maintainers
promote `test` to `main` with the release workflow when changes are ready. Merging to `main` updates
the article index and the live site after the Taopedia rebuild finishes.

# Delegate Stake

Delegate stake is the TAO a Bittensor delegate stakes themselves. It is the self-staked portion of
the delegate's staking context, not the full amount of TAO that may be associated with that delegate
after nomination
([Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Glossary: Delegate](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate)).

## What It Represents

A delegate is a validator that can receive stake from nominators. Delegate stake belongs to the
delegate side of that relationship: nominated TAO can add to the delegate's broader staking context,
but it is not delegate stake because it did not come from the delegate themselves
([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Nominator](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#nominator)).

On netuid 1, examples illustrate one subnet's self-stake context. They should not be read as
representing production staking behavior on another network
([Bittensor Networks](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/concepts/bittensor-networks)).

## Distinction from Staking

Staking names the process of attaching TAO support to a validator hotkey. Delegate stake names only
the TAO a delegate stakes themselves rather than nominated support from others
([Glossary: Staking](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#staking),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Staking** — attaching TAO support to a validator hotkey.
- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO only.

## Distinction from Stake Weight

Delegate stake is the TAO a validator stakes from their own balance. Stake weight is the computed
influence measure used inside subnet consensus after self-stake and nominated support are combined
([Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight),
[Understanding Subnets: Validator stake weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/subnets/understanding-subnets#validator-stake-weight)).

- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO only.
- **Stake weight** — consensus influence derived from broader stake context.

## Distinction from Validator Take

Delegate stake names an amount behind a hotkey. Validator take names the share a validator keeps
from delegated-stake emissions before the remainder credits back to nominators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO behind the hotkey.
- **Validator take** — commission on delegated-stake returns at distribution.

## Distinction from Delegation

Delegation names nominated TAO attached to a validator hotkey. Delegate stake names only the TAO the
validator supplied from their own balance on the selected subnet
([Glossary: Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegation),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake)).

- **Delegation** — nominated TAO attached to a validator hotkey.
- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO only.

## Distinction from Nominator

A nominator supplies delegated support to a validator. Delegate stake is the validator's own
committed TAO rather than support from nominators
([Glossary: Nominator](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#nominator),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake)).

- **Nominator** — wallet role that supplies delegated support.
- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO on the receiving hotkey.

## Distinction from Effective Stake

Effective stake counts delegate-owned plus nominated TAO behind one hotkey. Delegate stake counts
only the self-supplied portion
([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Subnet Metagraph](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/subnets/metagraph)).

- **Effective stake** — combined self-stake plus nominated support behind the hotkey.
- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO only.

## Distinction from Stake

Stake names the validator-associated amount after support exists. Delegate stake names only the
validator-supplied portion of that amount
([Glossary: Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake),
[Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Stake** — combined validator-associated amount behind the position.
- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO only.

## Distinction from Yuma Consensus

Delegate stake names the TAO a validator stakes from their own balance behind a hotkey. Yuma
Consensus converts validator weight submissions into miner incentives and validator dividends at
tempo boundaries and does not by itself label which portion of TAO came from the validator
personally
([Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions)).

- **Delegate stake** — validator-supplied TAO behind the hotkey.
- **Yuma Consensus** — consensus process that turns validator weights into emission shares. Delegate
  stake names validator-supplied TAO; Yuma processes validator weights into rewards
  ([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

Stake weight combines self-stake and nominated support for consensus influence; delegate stake is
one input to that broader stake picture, not the full settlement pass
([Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight)).

## Reader Boundary

Delegate stake names the TAO a delegate stakes themselves, not nominated support, effective stake,
stake weight, or validator-selection advice
([Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake)).

## Distinction from Alpha Staker

Delegate stake and an alpha staker describe an amount and a participant. Delegate stake is stake a
holder assigns to a validator's hotkey for use in consensus and rewards, while an alpha staker is
any participant holding staked alpha in a subnet — a role that includes those who self-stake as well
as those who delegate
([Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake),
[Staking into Subnets](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation#staking-into-subnets),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Delegate stake** — stake assigned to a validator's hotkey for consensus.
- **Alpha staker** — any participant holding staked alpha in a subnet.

## Further Reading

- [Glossary: Delegate Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate-stake)
- [Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)
- [Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake)
- [Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight)

# Validator Take

Validator take is the share of delegated-stake emissions that a validator keeps before the remaining
emissions flow to stakers
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

The term is a distribution concept. It describes a split inside delegated-stake emissions after the
validator-side amount already exists, not the consensus step that produced that amount
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## What It Represents

Validator take concerns the portion of emissions tied to delegated stake on a selected subnet. On
netuid 1, the key relationship is between a validator and the stakers who delegated to it: the take
is the validator's kept share, and the remaining delegated-stake emissions flow to those stakers at
tempo distribution ([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Tempo](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#tempo),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Examples tied to netuid 1 illustrate one subnet's commission split. They should not be read as
representing production settings on another network
([Bittensor Networks](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/concepts/bittensor-networks)).

## Distinction from Subnet Owner Take

On a subnet such as netuid 1, validator take and subnet owner take name different emission slices.
Validator take is the percentage a validator keeps from delegated-stake dividends before the
remainder flows to nominators, while subnet owner take is the documented 18 percent share of subnet
alpha emissions routed to the subnet owner as stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Validator take** — validator–delegator split on validation dividends at tempo distribution.
- **Subnet owner take** — global owner cut from that subnet's emission bucket.

## Distinction from Child Hotkeys

Validator take names the commission rate on validation dividends on a subnet such as netuid 1, while
a child hotkey names the authorized key a parent delegate uses to perform validation with
re-delegated stake
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — fee applied when dividends split between validator and stakers.
- **Child hotkey** — worker identity that earns dividends under delegation.

## Distinction from Dividends

Validator take is the share of validator dividends kept by the validator hotkey. Dividends are the
validator-side reward stream produced from subnet emissions before that split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Dividends](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#emission)).

- **Dividends** — validator-side payout category consensus produces.
- **Validator take** — configured share kept from the delegated-stake portion at distribution.

## Distinction from Childkey Take

A child hotkey carries its own take rate, the [[Childkey Take]], which applies at a different point
in the dividend flow. Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from emissions tied to
delegated stake before the remainder reaches delegators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Child Hotkeys](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/validators/child-hotkeys)).

- **Validator take** — split between validator and its delegators.
- **[[Childkey Take]]** — split between parent hotkey and child hotkey validating on its behalf.

## Distinction from Validator Permit

Validator take is the commission on delegated-stake dividends. A validator permit is the on-chain
right to submit counting weights and take part in consensus
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Validator Permit](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-permit)).

- **Validator permit** — right to submit counting weights before dividends exist.
- **Validator take** — commission applied once delegated-stake dividends are credited.

## Distinction from Effective Stake

Effective stake is the combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey. Validator take is the
commission rate applied when delegated-emission returns are split at distribution
([Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Effective stake** — combined staking total behind a delegate hotkey.
- **Validator take** — commission rate on delegated returns at distribution.

## Distinction from Nominator

A nominator delegates TAO to a validator hotkey. Validator take names what share of
delegated-emission returns the validator keeps before the remainder flows to those nominators
([Glossary: Nominator](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#nominator),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Nominator** — role that supplies delegated support.
- **Validator take** — configured share the validator keeps before the remainder flows to stakers.

## Distinction from Delegation Rewards

Validator take is the commission a validator keeps from delegated-emission returns before nominators
receive the remainder, while delegation rewards are what remains for delegated stake after that
split
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Staking and delegation overview](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Validator take** — cut taken off the top of delegated returns.
- **Delegation rewards** — portion that reaches nominators afterward.

## Distinction from Emission Split

Validator take is not a fourth headline share in the emission split. It is the cut a validator keeps
from delegated stake inside the validator-and-staker bucket after that bucket is credited
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

- **Emission split** — role proportions credited at tempo end.
- **Validator take** — commission applied inside the validator-and-staker bucket.

## Distinction from Incentives

[Incentives](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#incentives) name miner-side emission
outcomes produced from clipped and aggregated weight signals. Validator take names the configured
share a validator keeps when the delegated-stake portion is later split
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus)).

- **Incentives** — miner-side emission outcomes from consensus.
- **Validator take** — validator commission on delegated-stake dividends at distribution.

## Distinction from Yuma Consensus

Validator take is the configurable commission a validator keeps from delegated-stake emissions at
distribution. It names a post-settlement split rule inside the staking relationship, not the
consensus mechanism that builds validator dividend shares from weight submissions
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

Yuma Consensus is the on-chain mechanism that runs at the epoch boundary on the selected netuid. It
reads the weight matrix from eligible validators, applies clipping and bonding, and converts the
result into miner incentives and validator dividend shares
([Yuma Consensus](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus),
[Emission](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions)).

Yuma produces the validator-side dividend pool from consensus; validator take applies afterward when
the delegated-stake portion is split between validator and nominators. Settlement and commission are
separate stages on the same emission path
([Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions),
[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).

Readers should not read a higher take percentage as proof of stronger weight influence—that is stake
weight vocabulary. Take only governs how delegated dividends are shared after Yuma settles.

- **Validator take** — commission on delegated-stake validator emissions at distribution.
- **Yuma Consensus** — epoch-boundary settlement from validator weights to emission shares.

## Distinction from Staking

Validator take belongs to the staking relationship between a validator and the stakers who support
that validator. Delegation describes the support relationship, while validator take describes the
validator-kept share of the delegated-stake emissions
([Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation),
[Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)).

- **Delegate stake / effective stake** — stake context around a validator.
- **Validator take** — how the delegated-stake emission share is split at distribution.

## Reader Boundary

Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).

## Distinction from Delegate

Validator take and delegate name a fee and the party that charges it. A delegate is a validator that
accepts stake from nominators and validates on their behalf, while validator take is the percentage
that delegate keeps from the rewards generated on delegated stake before the remainder is paid to
nominators
([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
[Glossary: Delegate](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#delegate),
[Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)).

- **Delegate** — a validator that accepts stake from nominators.
- **Validator take** — the commission that delegate keeps from delegated-stake rewards.

## Further Reading

- [Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-)
- [Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)
- [Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)
- [Delegation](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/staking-and-delegation/delegation)

@@ -42,6 +42,25 @@
 representing production settings on another network
 ([Bittensor Networks](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/concepts/bittensor-networks)).
 
+## Validator Take Is Not Stake Weight
+
+Validator take is a distribution split. It tells you how validator-side emissions or dividends are
+shared after that validator-side amount already exists, not how that amount was created
+([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
+[Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions),
+[Emission: Distribution](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/emissions#distribution)).
+
+Stake weight is different vocabulary. It describes validator influence in consensus and is tied to
+stake context such as [[Effective Stake]], not the fee split that later determines
+[[Delegation Rewards]]
+([Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight),
+[Understanding Subnets: Validator stake weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/subnets/understanding-subnets#validator-stake-weight),
+[Glossary: Effective Stake](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#effective-stake)).
+
+[[Yuma Consensus]] produces validator-side emissions first. Validator take applies afterward when
+those emissions are split between the validator and delegators. It is not a measure of validator
+influence in consensus.
+
 ## Distinction from Subnet Owner Take
 
 On a subnet such as netuid 1, validator take and subnet owner take name different emission slices.
@@ -185,13 +204,18 @@
 - **Delegate stake / effective stake** — stake context around a validator.
 - **Validator take** — how the delegated-stake emission share is split at distribution.
 
-## Reader Boundary
+## Reader Shortcut
 
-Validator take should be read as reference vocabulary for emission distribution. It is not a
-recommendation, validator quality score, or complete explanation of staking outcomes
+If the question is "how do rewards get split after they already exist?", read validator take and
+[[Delegation Rewards]]. If the question is "which validator has more weight in consensus?", read
+[[Effective Stake]] and [[Yuma Consensus]]
 ([Glossary: Validator Take %](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#validator-take-),
+[Glossary: Stake Weight](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/resources/glossary#stake-weight),
 [Yuma Consensus: Validator emissions](https://docs.learnbittensor.org/learn/yuma-consensus#validator-emissions)).
 
+A higher take changes the validator-versus-staker payout split. It does not by itself mean higher
+stake weight, stronger consensus influence, or better validator performance.
+
 ## Distinction from Delegate
 
 Validator take and delegate name a fee and the party that charges it. A delegate is a validator that

Updated [content/pages/validator_take/index.mdx](/home/ubuntu/Videos/study/PromptForge/runs/e35ventura__taopedia-articles-20260628T200828Z/tasks/clarify-validator-take-vs-stake-weight/generated/workspace/content/pages/validator_take/index.mdx) with the required `## Validator Take Is Not Stake Weight` and `## Reader Shortcut` sections. The article now states that validator take is a post-emission distribution split, applies after validator-side emissions/dividends already exist, and is not a measure of consensus influence. It also includes `[[Delegation Rewards]]`, `[[Effective Stake]]`, and `[[Yuma Consensus]]` with primary-source citations for validator take and stake weight vocabulary.

I did not run repo validation commands.
